**Action:** `get_current_board`

### Step 2: Analyze the Board and Identify Key Elements
Once I have the board state, I'll analyze it to:
- **Identify Weaknesses**: Look for exposed pawns, isolated pieces, or weak squares that White might be targeting.
- **Evaluate Piece Activity**: Determine which of my pieces are active and which are passive. Active pieces (like knights and bishops) often have more strategic value.
- **Consider Pawn Structure**: Analyze the pawn structure to see if there are any opportunities for pawn storms or defensive solidification.

### Step 3: Generate Legal Moves
With a clear understanding of the board, I'll generate all legal moves available to Black. This will help me evaluate each option and choose the best one.

**Action:** `get_legal_moves`

### Step 4: Evaluate and Choose the Best Move
After generating the legal moves, I'll evaluate each one based on:
- **Tactical Threats**: Identify any immediate threats or tactical combinations that can gain material or create a significant advantage.
- **Strategic Goals**: Consider long-term strategic goals such as controlling key squares, developing pieces, and preparing for future attacks.

### Example Analysis (Hypothetical Board State)
Let's assume the board state is as follows:
- White has just moved `e4`, creating a center pawn weakness.
- Black's kingside knight (`d6`) is well-placed but not actively developing.

- `Nd5`
- `Bg4`

- `Bxd4+`

### Choosing the Best Move
Given the hypothetical board state, I would evaluate each move:
- **`Nc6`**: This move develops the knight and controls a key central square. It also prepares for potential future moves like `e5`.
- **`Nd5`**: This move targets White's pawn on `e4`, potentially weakening it further.
- **`Bg4`**: This move attacks White's kingside, putting pressure on the queenside and preparing for a future bishop pair advantage.
- **`Bb7`**: This move controls a key central square and supports potential future moves like `e5`.
- **`Bxd4+`**: This move captures the pawn but leaves Black's kingside weak to attack.

### Best Move: `Nc6`
Based on this analysis, I would choose:
**Action:** `make_move Nc6`

This move develops the knight and controls a key central square, preparing for future development and potential counterattacks. It also maintains flexibility in terms of further moves like `e5`.

**Action:** `get_current_board`

### Step 2: Analyze Legal Moves

**Action:** `get_legal_moves`

**Action:** `make_move <Uci formatted move>`

6. **Client (AI Model):** `make_move <Uci formatted move>`

8. **Client (AI Model):** Continues to play, repeating the process as needed.
